      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RCEP_GDP.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="359" data-file-width="377" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/RCEP_GDP.png/250px-RCEP_GDP.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/RCEP_GDP.png/375px-RCEP_GDP.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0f/RCEP_GDP.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RCEP_GDP.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         NAFTA GDP – 2012 : IMF – World Economic Outlook Databases (Oct 2013)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        North American Free Trade Agreement
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        NAFTA
       </b>
       ; Spanish:
       <i>
        Tratado de Libre Comercio de América del Norte
       </i>
       ,
       <b>
        TLCAN
       </b>
       ; French:
       <i>
        Accord de libre-échange nord-américain
       </i>
       ,
       <b>
        ALÉNA
       </b>
       ) is an agreement signed by
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       , creating a trilateral
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_bloc" title="Trade bloc">
        trade bloc
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
        North America
       </a>
       . The agreement came into force on January 1, 1994.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It superseded the
       <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada–United States Free Trade Agreement">
        Canada–United States Free Trade Agreement
       </a>
       between the U.S. and Canada.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       NAFTA has two supplements: the
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Agreement_on_Environmental_Cooperation" title="North American Agreement on Environmental Cooperation">
        North American Agreement on Environmental Cooperation
       </a>
       (NAAEC) and the North American Agreement on Labor Cooperation (NAALC).
      </p>
      <p>
       Most economic analyses indicate that NAFTA has been beneficial to the North American economies and the average citizen,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:9-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but harmed a small minority of workers in industries exposed to trade competition.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Economists hold that withdrawing from NAFTA or renegotiating NAFTA in a way that reestablishes
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_barrier" title="Trade barrier">
        trade barriers
       </a>
       will adversely affect the U.S. economy and cost jobs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:8-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:10-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:11-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Though Mexico would be much more affected severely by job loss and reduction of economic growth over both the short and long term.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>

      <h2>
       <span id="Negotiation.2C_Ratification.2C_and_Revision">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Negotiation,_Ratification,_and_Revision">
        Negotiation, Ratification, and Revision
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nafta.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="481" data-file-width="715" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nafta.jpg/270px-Nafta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nafta.jpg/405px-Nafta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nafta.jpg/540px-Nafta.jpg 2x" width="270"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nafta.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Back row, left to right: Mexican President
         <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Salinas_de_Gortari" title="Carlos Salinas de Gortari">
          Carlos Salinas de Gortari
         </a>
         , U.S. President
         <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">
          George H. W. Bush
         </a>
         , and Canadian Prime Minister
         <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mulroney" title="Brian Mulroney">
          Brian Mulroney
         </a>
         , at the initialing of the draft North American Free Trade Agreement in October 1992. In front are Mexican Secretary of Commerce and Industrial Development
         <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Serra_Puche" title="Jaime Serra Puche">
          Jaime Serra Puche
         </a>
         , United States Trade Representative
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carla_Hills" title="Carla Hills">
          Carla Hills
         </a>
         , and Canadian Minister of International Trade
         <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wilson_(Canadian_politician)" title="Michael Wilson (Canadian politician)">
          Michael Wilson
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The impetus for a North American free trade zone began with U. S. President
       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">
        Ronald Reagan
       </a>
       , who made the idea part of his campaign when he announced his candidacy for the presidency in November 1979.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAFTAcdnEncyc_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NAFTAcdnEncyc-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Canada and the United States signed the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada-United_States_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada-United States Free Trade Agreement">
        Canada-United States Free Trade Agreement
       </a>
       (FTA) in 1988, and shortly afterward Mexican President
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Salinas_de_Gortari" title="Carlos Salinas de Gortari">
        Carlos Salinas de Gortari
       </a>
       decided to approach US president
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" title="George H.W. Bush">
        George H.W. Bush
       </a>
       to propose a similar agreement in an effort to bring in foreign investment following the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_debt_crisis" title="Latin American debt crisis">
        Latin American debt crisis
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAFTAcdnEncyc_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NAFTAcdnEncyc-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the two leaders began negotiating, the Canadian government under Prime Minister
       <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mulroney" title="Brian Mulroney">
        Brian Mulroney
       </a>
       feared that the advantages Canada had gained through the Canada-US FTA would be undermined by a US-Mexican bilateral agreement, and asked to become a party to the US-Mexican talks.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canworld_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-canworld-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following diplomatic negotiations dating back to 1990 among the three nations, the three leaders signed the agreement in their respective capitals on December 17, 1992.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The signed agreement then needed to be
       <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">
        ratified
       </a>
       by each nation's legislative or parliamentary branch.
      </p>
      <p>
       The earlier
       <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada–United States Free Trade Agreement">
        Canada–United States Free Trade Agreement
       </a>
       had been controversial and divisive in Canada, and featured as an issue in the
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_federal_election,_1988" title="Canadian federal election, 1988">
        1988 Canadian election
       </a>
       . In that election, more Canadians voted for anti-free trade parties (the
       <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Canada" title="Liberal Party of Canada">
        Liberals
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_(Canada)" title="New Democratic Party (Canada)">
        New Democrats
       </a>
       ) but the split of the votes between the two parties meant that the pro-free trade
       <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Progressive Conservative Party of Canada">
        Progressive Conservatives
       </a>
       (PCs) came out of the election with the most seats and so took power. Mulroney and the PCs had a
       <a href="/wiki/Majority_government" title="Majority government">
        parliamentary majority
       </a>
       easily passed the 1987 Canada-U.S. FTA and NAFTA bills. However, Mulroney was replaced as Conservative leader and prime minister by
       <a href="/wiki/Kim_Campbell" title="Kim Campbell">
        Kim Campbell
       </a>
       . Campbell led the PC party into the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1993_Canadian_election" title="1993 Canadian election">
        1993 election
       </a>
       where they were decimated by the Liberal Party under
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Chr%C3%A9tien" title="Jean Chrétien">
        Jean Chrétien
       </a>
       , who campaigned on a promise to renegotiate or abrogate NAFTA. Chrétien subsequently negotiated two supplemental agreements with Bush, who had subverted the LAC
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       advisory process
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and worked to "fast track" the signing prior to the end of his term, ran out of time and had to pass the required ratification and signing of the implementation law to incoming president
       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">
        Bill Clinton
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Before sending it to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">
        United States Senate
       </a>
       Clinton added two side agreements, the North American Agreement on Labor Cooperation (NAALC) and the
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Agreement_on_Environmental_Cooperation" title="North American Agreement on Environmental Cooperation">
        North American Agreement on Environmental Cooperation
       </a>
       (NAAEC), to protect workers and the environment, and also allay the concerns of many House members. They also required U.S. partners to adhere to environmental practices and regulations similar to its own.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       After much consideration and emotional discussion, the US
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives" title="House of Representatives">
        House of Representatives
       </a>
       passed the North American Free Trade Agreement Implementation Act on November 17, 1993, 234–200. The agreement's supporters included 132 Republicans and 102 Democrats. The bill passed the Senate on November 20, 1993, 61–38.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Senate supporters were 34 Republicans and 27 Democrats. Clinton signed it into law on December 8, 1993; the agreement went into effect on January 1, 1994.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Clinton, while signing the NAFTA bill, stated that "NAFTA means jobs. American jobs, and good-paying American jobs. If I didn't believe that, I wouldn't support this agreement."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       NAFTA then replaced the previous Canada-US FTA.
      </p>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">

         </a>

          <i>
           Problems playing these files? See
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Provisions">
        Provisions
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The goal of NAFTA was to eliminate barriers to trade and investment between the U.S., Canada and Mexico. The implementation of NAFTA on January 1, 1994 brought the immediate elimination of
       <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">
        tariffs
       </a>
       on more than one-half of Mexico's
       <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">
        exports
       </a>
       to the U.S. and more than one-third of U.S. exports to Mexico. Within 10 years of the implementation of the agreement, all U.S.-Mexico tariffs were to be eliminated except for some U.S. agricultural exports to Mexico to be phased out within 15 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most U.S.-Canada trade was already duty-free. NAFTA also sought to eliminate non-
       <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">
        tariff
       </a>
       trade barriers and to protect the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intellectual_property_rights" title="Intellectual property rights">
        intellectual property rights
       </a>
       on traded
       <a href="/wiki/Product_(business)" title="Product (business)">
        products
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Chapter 52 provides a procedure for the international resolution of disputes over the application and interpretation of NAFTA. It was modeled after Chapter 69 of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada-United_States_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada-United States Free Trade Agreement">
        Canada-United States Free Trade Agreement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="external text" href="https://www.nafta-sec-alena.org/Default.aspx?tabid=96&amp;language=en-US" rel="nofollow">
        roster of NAFTA adjudicators
       </a>
       includes many retired judges, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Alice_Desjardins" title="Alice Desjardins">
        Alice Desjardins
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/John_Maxwell_Evans" title="John Maxwell Evans">
        John Maxwell Evans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Constance_Hunt" title="Constance Hunt">
        Constance Hunt
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/John_Richard" title="John Richard">
        John Richard
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arlin_M._Adams" title="Arlin M. Adams">
        Arlin M. Adams
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Susan_Christine_O%27Meara_Getzendanner" title="Susan Christine O'Meara Getzendanner">
        Susan Getzendanner
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/George_C._Pratt" title="George C. Pratt">
        George C. Pratt
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Byron_Renfrew" title="Charles Byron Renfrew">
        Charles B. Renfrew
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Day_O%27Connor" title="Sandra Day O'Connor">
        Sandra Day O'Connor
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Intellectual_property">
        Intellectual property
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The North American Free Trade Agreement Implementation Act made some changes to the
       <a href="/wiki/Copyright_law_of_the_United_States" title="Copyright law of the United States">
        copyright law of the United States
       </a>
       , foreshadowing the
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_Round_Agreements_Act" title="Uruguay Round Agreements Act">
        Uruguay Round Agreements Act
       </a>
       of 1994 by restoring
       <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">
        copyright
       </a>
       (within the NAFTA nations) on certain motion pictures which had entered the
       <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">
        public domain
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">
        Environment
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       U.S. congressional approval for NAFTA would have been impossible without addressing public concerns about NAFTA’s environmental impact.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RothbardAustria_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-RothbardAustria-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Clinton administration negotiated a side agreement on the environment with Canada and Mexico, the
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Agreement_on_Environmental_Cooperation" title="North American Agreement on Environmental Cooperation">
        North American Agreement on Environmental Cooperation
       </a>
       (NAAEC), which led to the creation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Commission_for_Environmental_Cooperation" title="Commission for Environmental Cooperation">
        Commission for Environmental Cooperation
       </a>
       (CEC) in 1994. To alleviate concerns that NAFTA, the first regional trade agreement between a
       <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">
        developing country
       </a>
       and two developed countries, would have negative
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_impact" title="Environmental impact">
        environmental impacts
       </a>
       , the commission was mandated to conduct ongoing
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ex_post" title="Ex post">
         ex post
        </a>
       </i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_assessment" title="Environmental assessment">
        environmental assessment
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It created one of the first
       <i>
        ex post
       </i>
       frameworks for environmental assessment of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_liberalization" title="Trade liberalization">
        trade liberalization
       </a>
       , designed to produce a
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Body_of_evidence&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Body of evidence (page does not exist)">
        body of evidence
       </a>
       with respect to the initial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypotheses" title="Hypotheses">
        hypotheses
       </a>
       about NAFTA and the environment, such as the concern that NAFTA would create a "
       <a href="/wiki/Race_to_the_bottom" title="Race to the bottom">
        race to the bottom
       </a>
       " in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_regulation" title="Environmental regulation">
        environmental regulation
       </a>
       among the three countries, or that NAFTA would pressure governments to increase their
       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_protection" title="Environmental protection">
        environmental protections
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The CEC has held
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2017)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       four symposia to evaluate the environmental impacts of NAFTA and commissioned 47 papers on the subject from leading independent experts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">
        Agriculture
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       From the earliest negotiation,
       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">
        agriculture
       </a>
       was (and still is) a controversial topic within NAFTA, as it has been with almost all
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_trade_agreement" title="Free trade agreement">
        free trade agreements
       </a>
       signed within the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        WTO
       </a>
       framework. Agriculture is the only section that was not negotiated trilaterally; instead, three separate agreements were signed between each pair of parties. The Canada–U.S. agreement contains significant restrictions and
       <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">
        tariff
       </a>
       quotas on agricultural products (mainly sugar, dairy, and poultry products), whereas the Mexico–U.S. pact allows for a wider
       <a href="/wiki/Liberalization" title="Liberalization">
        liberalization
       </a>
       within a framework of phase-out periods (it was the first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North-South_divide" title="North-South divide">
        North–South
       </a>
       FTA on agriculture to be signed).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_infrastructure">
        Transportation infrastructure
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       NAFTA established the
       <a href="/wiki/CANAMEX_Corridor" title="CANAMEX Corridor">
        CANAMEX Corridor
       </a>
       for road transport between Canada and Mexico, also proposed for use by rail, pipeline, and
       <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">
        fiber optic
       </a>
       telecommunications infrastructure. This became a High Priority Corridor under the U.S.
       <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_Surface_Transportation_Efficiency_Act" title="Intermodal Surface Transportation Efficiency Act">
        Intermodal Surface Transportation Efficiency Act
       </a>
       of 1991.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">
        Impact
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Obama,_Pe%C3%B1a_y_Harper._IX_Cumbre_de_L%C3%ADderes_de_Am%C3%A9rica_del_Norte.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Obama%2C_Pe%C3%B1a_y_Harper._IX_Cumbre_de_L%C3%ADderes_de_Am%C3%A9rica_del_Norte.jpg/250px-Obama%2C_Pe%C3%B1a_y_Harper._IX_Cumbre_de_L%C3%ADderes_de_Am%C3%A9rica_del_Norte.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Obama%2C_Pe%C3%B1a_y_Harper._IX_Cumbre_de_L%C3%ADderes_de_Am%C3%A9rica_del_Norte.jpg/375px-Obama%2C_Pe%C3%B1a_y_Harper._IX_Cumbre_de_L%C3%ADderes_de_Am%C3%A9rica_del_Norte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Obama%2C_Pe%C3%B1a_y_Harper._IX_Cumbre_de_L%C3%ADderes_de_Am%C3%A9rica_del_Norte.jpg/500px-Obama%2C_Pe%C3%B1a_y_Harper._IX_Cumbre_de_L%C3%ADderes_de_Am%C3%A9rica_del_Norte.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Obama,_Pe%C3%B1a_y_Harper._IX_Cumbre_de_L%C3%ADderes_de_Am%C3%A9rica_del_Norte.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Obama, Peña Nieto and Harper at the IX
         <a href="/wiki/North_American_Leaders%27_Summit" title="North American Leaders' Summit">
          North American Leaders' Summit
         </a>
         (informally known as the
         <i>
          Three Amigos Summit
         </i>
         ) in
         <a href="/wiki/Toluca" title="Toluca">
          Toluca
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">
        Canada
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Like Mexico and the U.S., Canada received a modest positive economic benefit as measured by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">
        GDP
       </a>
       . Many declines did not materialize, and some industries like the furniture industry, which had expected to suffer, grew instead.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Canadian
       <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">
        manufacturing
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Employment" title="Employment">
        employment
       </a>
       held steady despite an international downward trend in developed countries.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       One of NAFTA's biggest economic effects on U.S.-Canada trade has been higher bilateral agricultural flows.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the year 2008 alone, Canadian
       <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">
        exports
       </a>
       to the United States and Mexico were at $381.3 billion, and
       <a href="/wiki/Import" title="Import">
        imports
       </a>
       from NAFTA were at $245.1 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2007 study found that NAFTA has "almost zero welfare impact on member and nonmember countries."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A 2015 study found that Canada's welfare decreased by 0.06% as a result of the NAFTA tariff reductions, and that Canada's intra-bloc trade increased by 11%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_NAFTA_on_Mexico" title="Effects of NAFTA on Mexico">
        Effects of NAFTA on Mexico
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Maquiladora" title="Maquiladora">
        Maquiladoras
       </a>
       (Mexican assembly plants that take in imported components and produce
       <a href="/wiki/Good" title="Good">
        goods
       </a>
       for export) have become the landmark of trade in Mexico. They moved to Mexico from the United States
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       , hence the debate over the loss of American jobs. Income in the maquiladora sector has increased 15.5% since the implementation of NAFTA in 1994.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hufbauer_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hufbauer-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other sectors now benefit from the free trade agreement, and the share of
       <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">
        exports
       </a>
       to the US from non-border states has increased in the last five years
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2017)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       while the share of exports from border states has decreased. This has allowed rapid growth in non-border
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">
        metropolitan areas
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Toluca" title="Toluca">
        Toluca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Guanajuato" title="León, Guanajuato">
        León
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puebla,_Puebla" title="Puebla, Puebla">
        Puebla
       </a>
       ; all larger in population than
       <a href="/wiki/Tijuana" title="Tijuana">
        Tijuana
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Ciudad Juárez">
        Ciudad Juárez
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Reynosa" title="Reynosa">
        Reynosa
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The overall effect of the Mexico–U.S. agricultural agreement is disputed. Mexico did not invest in the
       <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">
        infrastructure
       </a>
       necessary for competition, such as efficient railroads and highways.This resulted in more difficult living conditions for the country's poor. Mexico's agricultural exports increased 9.4 percent annually between 1994 and 2001, while imports increased by only 6.9 percent a year during the same period.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One of the most affected agricultural sectors is the
       <a href="/wiki/Meat_industry" title="Meat industry">
        meat industry
       </a>
       . Mexico went from a small player in the pre-1994 U.S. export market to the second largest importer of U.S. agricultural products in 2004, and NAFTA may be a major catalyst for this change. Free trade removed the hurdles that impeded business between the two countries, so Mexico has provided a growing market for meat for the U.S., and increased sales and
       <a href="/wiki/Profit_(economics)" title="Profit (economics)">
        profits
       </a>
       for the U.S. meat industry. A coinciding noticeable increase in the Mexican
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Per_capita_GDP" title="Per capita GDP">
        per capita GDP
       </a>
       greatly changed meat consumption patterns; per capita meat consumption has grown.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Production of
       <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">
        corn
       </a>
       in Mexico has increased since NAFTA. But internal
       <a href="/wiki/Demand" title="Demand">
        demand
       </a>
       for corn has increased beyond Mexico's supply, and imports have become needed, far beyond the quotas Mexico originally negotiated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Zahniser &amp; Coyle also point out that corn prices in Mexico, adjusted for international prices, have drastically decreased, but through a program of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subsidies" title="Subsidies">
        subsidies
       </a>
       expanded by former president
       <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Fox" title="Vicente Fox">
        Vicente Fox
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Production_(economics)" title="Production (economics)">
        production
       </a>
       has remained stable since 2000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Reducing agricultural subsidies, especially corn subsidies, has been suggested as a way to reduce harms to Mexican farmers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2001
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Economic_Perspectives" title="Journal of Economic Perspectives">
         Journal of Economic Perspectives
        </a>
       </i>
       review of the existing literature found that NAFTA was a net benefit to Mexico.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the year 2003, 80% of the commerce in Mexico was executed only with the U.S. The commercial sales surplus, combined with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_budget_deficit" title="Government budget deficit">
        deficit
       </a>
       with the rest of the world, created a dependency in Mexico's exports. These effects were evident in 2001–2003; the result of that
       <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">
        recession
       </a>
       was either a low rate or a negative rate in Mexico's exports.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2015 study found that Mexico's welfare increased by 1.31% as a result of the NAFTA tariff reductions, and that Mexico's intra-bloc trade increased by 118%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">
        Inequality
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">
        poverty
       </a>
       fell in the most
       <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">
        globalization
       </a>
       -affected regions of Mexico.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       2013 and 2015 studies show that Mexican small farmers benefitted more from NAFTA than large-scale farmers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       NAFTA has also been credited with the rise of the Mexican
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">
        middle class
       </a>
       . A
       <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">
        Tufts University
       </a>
       study found that NAFTA lowered the average cost of basic necessities in Mexico by up to 50%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shannon_O_Neil_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Shannon_O_Neil-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This price reduction increased cash-on-hand for many Mexican families, allowing Mexico to graduate more engineers than
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       each year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashTimesNaftaGood_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WashTimesNaftaGood-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Growth in new sales orders indicates an increase in demand for manufactured products, which resulted in expansion of production and a higher
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Employment_rate" title="Employment rate">
        employment rate
       </a>
       to satisfy the increment in the demand. The growth in the maquiladora industry and in the manufacturing industry was of 4.7% in August 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Three quarters of the imports and exports comes are with the U.S.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">
        Tufts University
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_scientist" title="Political scientist">
        political scientist
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_W._Drezner" title="Daniel W. Drezner">
        Daniel W. Drezner
       </a>
       has argued that NAFTA made it easier for Mexico to transform to a real democracy and become a country that views itself as North American. This has boosted cooperation between the United States and Mexico.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:7-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">
        United States
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Economists consider that NAFTA was beneficial for the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In a 2012 survey of leading economists, 95% said that on average U.S. citizens benefited from NAFTA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:9-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A 2001
       <i>
        Journal of Economic Perspectives
       </i>
       review found that NAFTA was a net benefit to the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A 2015 study found that US welfare increased by 0.08% as a result of NAFTA tariff reductions, and that US intra-bloc trade increased by 41%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_36-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2015, the
       <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Research_Service" title="Congressional Research Service">
        Congressional Research Service
       </a>
       concluded that the "net overall effect of NAFTA on the U.S. economy appears to have been relatively modest, primarily because trade with Canada and Mexico accounts for a small percentage of U.S.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">
        GDP
       </a>
       . However, there were worker and firm adjustment costs as the three countries adjusted to more open trade and investment among their economies." The report also estimated that NAFTA added $80 billion to the US economy since its implementation, equivalent to a 0.5% increase in US GDP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Chamber_of_Commerce" title="U.S. Chamber of Commerce">
        U.S. Chamber of Commerce
       </a>
       credits NAFTA with increasing U.S. trade in goods and services with Canada and Mexico from $337 billion in 1993 to $1.2 trillion in 2011, while the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AFL-CIO" title="AFL-CIO">
        AFL-CIO
       </a>
       blames the agreement for sending 700,000 American manufacturing jobs to Mexico over that time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       University of California, San Diego economics professor
       <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Hanson" title="Gordon Hanson">
        Gordon Hanson
       </a>
       has said that NAFTA helped the U.S. compete against China and therefore saved U.S. jobs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:4-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:5-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While some jobs were lost to Mexico as a result of NAFTA, considerably more would have been lost to China if not for NAFTA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_55-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:4-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_56-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:5-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_balances">
        Trade balances
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The U.S. had a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_surplus" title="Trade surplus">
        trade surplus
       </a>
       with NAFTA countries of $28.3 billion for services in 2009 and a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_deficit" title="Trade deficit">
        trade deficit
       </a>
       of $94.6 billion (36.4% annual increase) for goods in 2010. This trade deficit accounted for 26.8 percent of all U.S. goods trade deficit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ustrstats_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ustrstats-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A study published in the August 2008 issue of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/American_Journal_of_Agricultural_Economics" title="American Journal of Agricultural Economics">
         American Journal of Agricultural Economics
        </a>
       </i>
       , found NAFTA increased U.S. agricultural exports to Mexico and Canada, even though most of the increase occurred a decade after its ratification. The study focused on the effects that gradual "phase-in" periods in regional trade agreements, including NAFTA, have on
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Trade_flow&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Trade flow (page does not exist)">
        trade flows
       </a>
       . Most of the increase in members’ agricultural trade, which was only recently brought under the purview of the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        World Trade Organization
       </a>
       , was due to very high trade barriers before NAFTA or other regional trade agreements.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Investment">
        Investment
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The U.S.
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">
        foreign direct investment
       </a>
       (FDI) in NAFTA countries (stock) was $327.5 billion in 2009 (latest data available)
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2017)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       , up 8.8% from 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ustrstats_57-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ustrstats-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The U.S. direct investment in NAFTA countries is in nonbank
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holding_companies" title="Holding companies">
        holding companies
       </a>
       , and in the manufacturing,
       <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">
        finance
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">
        insurance
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">
        mining
       </a>
       sectors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ustrstats_57-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ustrstats-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">
        foreign direct investment
       </a>
       of Canada and Mexico in the United States (stock) was $237.2 billion in 2009 (the latest data available), up 16.5% from 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ustrstats_57-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-ustrstats-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Jobs">
        Jobs
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <i>
        For impacts specific to the United States, see
        <a href="/wiki/NAFTA%27s_effect_on_United_States_employment" title="NAFTA's effect on United States employment">
         NAFTA's effect on United States employment
        </a>
        .
       </i>
      </p>
      <p>
       Many American small businesses depend on exporting their products to Canada or Mexico under NAFTA. According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_United_States_Trade_Representative" title="Office of the United States Trade Representative">
        U.S. Trade Representative
       </a>
       , this trade supports over 140,000 small- and medium-sized businesses in the US.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_Policy_Institute" title="Economic Policy Institute">
        Economic Policy Institute
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">
        Michigan
       </a>
       and other states with high concentrations of manufacturing jobs were most affected by job loss due to NAFTA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       EPI economist Robert Scott estimates some 682,900 U.S. jobs have been "lost or displaced" as a result of the trade agreement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, other studies have found that NAFTA only had a modest impact on manufacturing employment, and that
       <a href="/wiki/Automation" title="Automation">
        automation
       </a>
       explains 87% of the losses in manufacturing jobs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">
        University of California
       </a>
       Berkeley professor of economics
       <a href="/wiki/J._Bradford_DeLong" title="J. Bradford DeLong">
        Brad DeLong
       </a>
       , NAFTA had an insignificant impact on US manufacturing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:6-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The adverse impact on manufacturing has been very exaggerated in US political discourse according to DeLong,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_64-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:6-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Harvard economist
       <a href="/wiki/Dani_Rodrik" title="Dani Rodrik">
        Dani Rodrik
       </a>
       agrees.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_2">
        Environment
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       For more details on this topic, see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAFTA%27s_Impact_on_the_Environment" title="NAFTA's Impact on the Environment">
        NAFTA's Impact on the Environment
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <p>
       According to a study in the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_International_Economics" title="Journal of International Economics">
         Journal of International Economics
        </a>
       </i>
       , NAFTA reduced pollution emitted by the US manufacturing sector: "On average, nearly two-thirds of the reductions in PM
       <sub>
        10
       </sub>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and SO
       <sub>
        2
       </sub>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas#Direct_greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas">
        emissions
       </a>
       from the U.S. manufacturing sector between 1994 and 1998 can be attributed to trade liberalization following NAFTA."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Club" title="Sierra Club">
        Sierra Club
       </a>
       , NAFTA contributed to large-scale, export-oriented
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farming" title="Farming">
        farming
       </a>
       , which led to the increased use of
       <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">
        fossil fuels
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">
        pesticides
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GMO" title="GMO">
        GMO
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       NAFTA also contributed to environmentally destructive mining practices in Mexico.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_67-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It prevented Canada from effectively regulating its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tar_sands" title="Tar sands">
        tar sands
       </a>
       industry, and created new legal avenues for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transnational_corporations" title="Transnational corporations">
        transnational corporations
       </a>
       to fight
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_legislation" title="Environmental legislation">
        environmental legislation
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_67-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:3-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In some cases, environmental policy was neglected in the wake of trade liberalization; in other cases, NAFTA's measures for investment protection, such as Chapter 11, and measures against non-tariff trade barriers threatened to discourage more vigorous environmental policy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most serious overall increases in
       <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">
        pollution
       </a>
       due to NAFTA were found in the
       <a href="/wiki/Base_metal" title="Base metal">
        base metals
       </a>
       sector, the Mexican
       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
        petroleum
       </a>
       sector, and the transportation equipment sector in the United States and Mexico, but not in Canada.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mobility_of_persons">
        Mobility of persons
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="Department of Homeland Security">
        Department of Homeland Security
       </a>
       Yearbook of Immigration Statistics, during fiscal year 2006 (i.e., October 2005 through September 2006), 73,880 foreign professionals (64,633 Canadians and 9,247 Mexicans) were admitted into the United States for temporary employment under NAFTA (i.e., in the
       <a href="/wiki/TN_status" title="TN status">
        TN status
       </a>
       ). Additionally, 17,321 of their family members (13,136 Canadians, 2,904 Mexicans, as well as a number of third-country nationals married to Canadians and Mexicans) entered the U.S. in the treaty national's dependent (TD) status.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because DHS counts the number of the new
       <a href="/wiki/Form_I-94" title="Form I-94">
        I-94 arrival records
       </a>
       filled at the border, and the TN-1 admission is valid for three years, the number of non-immigrants in TN status present in the U.S. at the end of the fiscal year is approximately equal to the number of admissions during the year. (A discrepancy may be caused by some TN entrants leaving the country or changing status before their three-year admission period has expired, while other immigrants admitted earlier may change their status
       <i>
        to
       </i>
       TN or TD, or extend TN status granted earlier).
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">
        International Organization for Migration
       </a>
       , deaths of migrants have been on the rise worldwide with 5,604 deaths in 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:12-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An increased number of undocumented farmworkers in California may be due to the initial passing of NAFTA
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Canadian authorities estimated that on December 1, 2006, 24,830 U.S. citizens and 15,219 Mexican citizens were in Canada as "foreign workers". These numbers include both entrants under NAFTA and those who entered under other provisions of Canadian immigration law.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New entries of foreign workers in 2006 totalled 16,841 U.S. citizens and 13,933 Mexicans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Disputes_and_controversies">
        Disputes and controversies
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1992_U.S._presidential_candidate_Ross_Perot">
        1992 U.S. presidential candidate Ross Perot
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the second 1992 presidential debate, Ross Perot argued:
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        We have got to stop sending jobs overseas. It's pretty simple: If you're paying $12, $13, $14 an hour for factory workers and you can move your factory south of the border, pay a dollar an hour for labor,...have no health care—that's the most expensive single element in making a car— have no environmental controls, no pollution controls and no retirement, and you don't care about anything but making money, there will be a
        <a href="/wiki/Giant_sucking_sound" title="Giant sucking sound">
         giant sucking sound
        </a>
        going south.
        <br/>
        ...when [Mexico's] jobs come up from a dollar an hour to six dollars an hour, and ours go down to six dollars an hour, and then it's leveled again. But in the meantime, you've wrecked the country with these kinds of deals.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
         <a href="#cite_note-75">
          [75]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       Perot ultimately lost the election, and the winner,
       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">
        Bill Clinton
       </a>
       , supported NAFTA, which went into effect on January 1, 1994.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_disputes">
        Legal disputes
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This article needs to be
          <b>
           updated
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (August 2009)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In 1996, the gasoline additive
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methylcyclopentadienyl_Manganese_Tricarbonyl" title="Methylcyclopentadienyl Manganese Tricarbonyl">
        MMT
       </a>
       was brought to Canada by
       <a href="/wiki/Ethyl_Corporation" title="Ethyl Corporation">
        Ethyl Corporation
       </a>
       , an American company when the Canadian federal government banned imports of the additive. The American company brought a claim under NAFTA Chapter 11 seeking US$201 million,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       from the Canadian federal government as well as the Canadian provinces under the
       <a href="/wiki/Agreement_on_Internal_Trade" title="Agreement on Internal Trade">
        Agreement on Internal Trade
       </a>
       (AIT). They argued that the additive had not been conclusively linked to any health dangers, and that the prohibition was damaging to their company. Following a finding that the ban was a violation of the AIT,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Canadian federal government repealed the ban and
       <a href="/wiki/Settlement_(litigation)" title="Settlement (litigation)">
        settled
       </a>
       with the American company for US$13 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Studies by Health and Welfare Canada (now
       <a href="/wiki/Health_Canada" title="Health Canada">
        Health Canada
       </a>
       ) on the health effects of MMT in fuel found no significant health effects associated with exposure to these exhaust emissions. Other Canadian researchers and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="U.S. Environmental Protection Agency">
        U.S. Environmental Protection Agency
       </a>
       disagreed citing studies that suggested possible nerve damage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The United States and Canada have argued for years over the United States' 27%
       <a href="/wiki/Duty" title="Duty">
        duty
       </a>
       on Canadian
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Softwood_lumber" title="Softwood lumber">
        softwood lumber
       </a>
       imports. Canada filed many motions to have the duty eliminated and the collected duties returned to Canada.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the United States lost an
       <a href="/wiki/Appeal" title="Appeal">
        appeal
       </a>
       before a NAFTA panel, it responded by saying "We are, of course, disappointed with the [NAFTA panel's] decision, but it will have no impact on the
       <a href="/wiki/Dumping_(pricing_policy)" title="Dumping (pricing policy)">
        anti-dumping
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Countervailing_duties" title="Countervailing duties">
        countervailing duty
       </a>
       orders." (Nick Lifton, spokesman for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Trade_Representative" title="United States Trade Representative">
        U.S. Trade Representative
       </a>
       Rob Portman)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On July 21, 2006, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_International_Trade" title="United States Court of International Trade">
        United States Court of International Trade
       </a>
       found that imposition of the duties was contrary to U.S. law.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Change_in_income_trust_taxation_not_expropriation">
        Change in income trust taxation not expropriation
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       On October 30, 2007, American citizens
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.guidestar.org/organizations/36-3978074/marvin-elaine-gottlieb-family-foundation.aspx" rel="nofollow">
        Marvin and Elaine Gottlieb
       </a>
       filed a Notice of Intent to Submit a Claim to Arbitration under NAFTA, claiming thousands of U.S. investors lost a total of $5 billion in the fall-out from the
       <a href="/wiki/Income_trust#The_Conservatives_propose_new_rules_for_income_trusts" title="Income trust">
        Conservative Government's
       </a>
       decision the previous year to change the
       <a href="/wiki/Tax_rate" title="Tax rate">
        tax rate
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/Income_trust" title="Income trust">
        income trusts
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_sector" title="Energy sector">
        energy sector
       </a>
       . On April 29, 2009, a determination was made that this change in
       <a href="/wiki/Tax_law" title="Tax law">
        tax law
       </a>
       was not
       <a href="/wiki/Expropriation" title="Expropriation">
        expropriation
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_on_Mexican_farmers">
        Impact on Mexican farmers
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Several studies have rejected NAFTA responsibility for depressing the incomes of poor corn farmers. The trend existed more than a decade before NAFTA existed. Also, maize production increased after 1994, and there wasn't a measurable impact on the price of Mexican corn because of subsidized
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2017)">
           who?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       corn from the United States. The studies agreed that the abolition of
       <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_policy_of_the_United_States" title="Agricultural policy of the United States">
        U.S. agricultural subsidies
       </a>
       would benefit Mexican farmers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Zapatista_Uprising_in_response_to_NAFTA_in_Chiapas.2C_Mexico">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Zapatista_Uprising_in_response_to_NAFTA_in_Chiapas,_Mexico">
        Zapatista Uprising in response to NAFTA in Chiapas, Mexico
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       For more details on this topic, see
       <a href="/wiki/Zapatista_Army_of_National_Liberation" title="Zapatista Army of National Liberation">
        Zapatista Army of National Liberation
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <p>
       Preparations for NAFTA included cancellation of Article 27 of Mexico's constitution, the cornerstone of
       <a href="/wiki/Emiliano_Zapata" title="Emiliano Zapata">
        Emiliano Zapata
       </a>
       's revolution in 1910–1919. Under the historic Article 27, Indian communal landholdings were protected from sale or
       <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">
        privatization
       </a>
       . However, this barrier to
       <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">
        investment
       </a>
       was incompatible with NAFTA. Indian farmers feared the loss of their remaining lands, and also feared cheap imports (substitutes) from the US. The
       <a href="/wiki/Zapatista_Army_of_National_Liberation" title="Zapatista Army of National Liberation">
        Zapatistas
       </a>
       labelled NAFTA a "death sentence" to Indian communities all over Mexico. Then
       <a href="/wiki/Zapatista_Army_of_National_Liberation" title="Zapatista Army of National Liberation">
        EZLN
       </a>
       declared war on the Mexican state on January 1, 1994, the day NAFTA came into force.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Chapter_11">
        Chapter 11
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Another contentious issue is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Investor_state_dispute_settlement" title="Investor state dispute settlement">
        investor state dispute settlement
       </a>
       obligations contained in Chapter 11 of NAFTA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chapter 11 allows
       <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">
        corporations
       </a>
       or individuals to sue Mexico, Canada or the United States for compensation when actions taken by those governments (or by those for whom they are responsible at
       <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">
        international law
       </a>
       , such as provincial, state, or municipal governments) violate international law.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This chapter has been criticized by groups in the U.S.,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mexico,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Canada
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       for a variety of reasons, including not taking into account important social and environmental
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       considerations. In Canada, several groups, including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Canadians" title="Council of Canadians">
        Council of Canadians
       </a>
       , challenged the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">
        constitutionality
       </a>
       of Chapter 11. They lost at the trial level
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and have subsequently appealed.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2017)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methanex_Corporation" title="Methanex Corporation">
        Methanex Corporation
       </a>
       , a Canadian corporation, filed a
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
        US$
       </a>
       970 million suit against the United States because, it said, a
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       ban on
       <a href="/wiki/Methyl_tert-butyl_ether" title="Methyl tert-butyl ether">
        Methyl tert-butyl ether
       </a>
       (MTBE), a substance that had found its way into many wells in the state, was hurtful to the corporation's sales of
       <a href="/wiki/Methanol" title="Methanol">
        methanol
       </a>
       . The claim was rejected, and the company was ordered to pay US$3 million to the U.S. government in costs, based on the following reasoning: "But as a matter of general international law, a non-discriminatory
       <a href="/wiki/Regulation" title="Regulation">
        regulation
       </a>
       for a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_purpose" title="Public purpose">
        public purpose
       </a>
       , which is enacted in accordance with
       <a href="/wiki/Due_process" title="Due process">
        due process
       </a>
       and, which affects,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inter_alios" title="Inter alios">
        inter alios
       </a>
       , a foreign investor or investment is not deemed expropriatory and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Compensable&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Compensable (page does not exist)">
        compensable
       </a>
       unless specific commitments had been given by the regulating government to the then putative foreign investor contemplating investment that the government would refrain from such regulation."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In another case,
       <a href="/wiki/Metalclad" title="Metalclad">
        Metalclad
       </a>
       , an American corporation, was awarded US$15.6 million from Mexico after a Mexican municipality refused a construction permit for the
       <a href="/wiki/Hazardous_waste" title="Hazardous waste">
        hazardous waste
       </a>
       landfill it intended to construct in
       <a href="/wiki/Guadalc%C3%A1zar,_San_Luis_Potos%C3%AD" title="Guadalcázar, San Luis Potosí">
        Guadalcázar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Potos%C3%AD" title="San Luis Potosí">
        San Luis Potosí
       </a>
       . The construction had already been approved by the federal government with various environmental requirements imposed (see paragraph 48 of the tribunal decision). The NAFTA panel found that the municipality did not have the authority to ban construction on the basis of its environmental concerns.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Eli_Lilly" title="Eli Lilly">
        Eli Lilly
       </a>
       and Company v. Government of Canada
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the plaintiff presented a US$500 million claim for the way Canada requires usefulness in its drug
       <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">
        patent
       </a>
       legislation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm24nov_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gm24nov-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Apotex" title="Apotex">
        Apotex
       </a>
       is sued the U.S. for US$520 million because of opportunity it says it lost in an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FDA" title="FDA">
        FDA
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Generic_drug" title="Generic drug">
        generic drug
       </a>
       decision.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm24nov_97-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gm24nov-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.wikinvest.com/stock/Lone_Pine_Resources" rel="nofollow">
        Lone Pine Resources Inc.
       </a>
       v. Government of Canada
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       filed a US$250 million claim against Canada, accusing it of "arbitrary, capricious and illegal" behaviour,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm22nov_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gm22nov-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       because Quebec intends to prevent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fracking" title="Fracking">
        fracking
       </a>
       exploration under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_Seaway" title="St. Lawrence Seaway">
        St. Lawrence Seaway
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm24nov_97-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-gm24nov-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.bennettjones.com/BarutciskiMilos/" rel="nofollow">
        Milos Barutciski
       </a>
       , the lawyer for Lone Pine, has decried portrayals of his client as "another rapacious multinational challenging governments’ ability to regulate for health, safety and the environment".
      </p>
      <p>
       Lone Pine Resources is incorporated in Delaware but headquartered in Calgary,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm22nov_99-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gm22nov-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and had an
       <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">
        initial public offering
       </a>
       on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NYSE" title="NYSE">
        NYSE
       </a>
       May 25, 2011 of 15 million shares each for $13, which raised US$195 million.
