       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Barutciski acknowledged "that NAFTA and other investor-protection treaties create an anomaly in that Canadian companies that have also seen their permits rescinded by the very same Quebec legislation, which expressly forbids the paying of compensation, do not have the right (to) pursue a NAFTA claim," and that winning "compensation in Canadian courts for domestic companies in this case would be more difficult since the Constitution puts
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Property_rights" title="Property rights">
        property rights
       </a>
       in provincial hands."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm22nov_99-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-gm22nov-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A treaty
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       with China would extend similar rights to Chinese investors, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government-owned_corporation" title="Government-owned corporation">
        SOEs
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gm22nov_99-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-gm22nov-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Chapter_19">
        Chapter 19
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Also contentious is NAFTA's Chapter 19, which subjects
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antidumping" title="Antidumping">
        antidumping
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Countervailing_duty" title="Countervailing duty">
        countervailing duty
       </a>
       (AD/CVD) determinations to binational panel review instead of, or in addition to, conventional judicial review.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Federal_Register_Millan_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Federal_Register_Millan-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For example, in the United States, review of agency decisions imposing antidumping and countervailing duties are normally heard before the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_International_Trade" title="United States Court of International Trade">
        U.S. Court of International Trade
       </a>
       , an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Article_I_and_Article_III_tribunals" title="Article I and Article III tribunals">
        Article III court
       </a>
       . NAFTA parties, however, have the option of appealing the decisions to binational panels composed of five citizens from the two relevant NAFTA countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Federal_Register_Millan_101-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Federal_Register_Millan-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The panelists are generally lawyers experienced in international trade law. Since NAFTA does not include substantive provisions concerning AD/CVD, the panel is charged with determining whether final agency determinations involving AD/CVD conform with the country's domestic law. Chapter 19 is an anomaly in international dispute settlement since it does not apply international law, but requires a panel composed of individuals from many countries to re-examine the application of one country's domestic law.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A Chapter 19 panel is expected to examine whether the agency's determination is supported by "substantial evidence". This standard assumes significant deference to the domestic agency. Some of the most controversial trade disputes in recent years, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_softwood_lumber_dispute" title="Canada–United States softwood lumber dispute">
        U.S.–Canada softwood lumber dispute
       </a>
       , have been litigated before Chapter 19 panels.
      </p>
      <p>
       Decisions by Chapter 19 panels can be challenged before a NAFTA extraordinary challenge committee. However, an extraordinary challenge committee does not function as an ordinary appeal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Federal_Register_Millan_101-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Federal_Register_Millan-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Under NAFTA, it will only vacate or remand a decision if the decision involves a significant and material error that threatens the integrity of the NAFTA dispute settlement system. Since January 2006, no NAFTA party has successfully challenged a Chapter 19 panel's decision before an extraordinary challenge committee.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_from_2016_U.S._presidential_candidates">
        Criticism from 2016 U.S. presidential candidates
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">
         60 Minutes
        </a>
       </i>
       interview in September 2015, American
       <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump_presidential_campaign,_2016" title="Donald Trump presidential campaign, 2016">
        2016 presidential candidate
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">
        Donald Trump
       </a>
       called NAFTA calling it "the single worst trade deal ever approved in [the United States]",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and said that if elected, he would "either renegotiate it, or we will break it".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_Pablo_Casta%C3%B1%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Juan Pablo Castañón (page does not exist)">
        Juan Pablo Castañón
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Casta%C3%B1%C3%B3n_Casta%C3%B1%C3%B3n" title="es:Juan Pablo Castañón Castañón">
         es
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       president of the trade group Consejo Coordinador Empresarial, expressed concern about renegotiation and the willingness to focus on the car industry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:03_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:03-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A range of trade experts have said that pulling out of NAFTA would have a range of
       <a href="/wiki/Unintended_consequences" title="Unintended consequences">
        unintended consequences
       </a>
       for the U.S., including reduced access to the its biggest
       <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">
        export
       </a>
       markets, a reduction in
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">
        economic growth
       </a>
       , and higher
       <a href="/wiki/Price" title="Price">
        prices
       </a>
       for gasoline, cars, fruits, and vegetables.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Members of the private initiative in Mexico noted that to eliminate NAFTA, many laws must be adapted by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress">
        U.S. Congress
       </a>
       . The move would also eventually result in legal complaints by the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        World Trade Organization
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:03_105-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:03-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Washington Post
       </i>
       noted that a
       <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Research_Service" title="Congressional Research Service">
        Congressional Research Service
       </a>
       review of academic literature concluded that the "net overall effect of NAFTA on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._economy" title="U.S. economy">
        U.S. economy
       </a>
       appears to have been relatively modest, primarily because
       <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">
        trade
       </a>
       with Canada and Mexico accounts for a small percentage of U.S.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">
        GDP
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_36-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Democratic candidate
       <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders" title="Bernie Sanders">
        Bernie Sanders
       </a>
       opposed the
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership" title="Trans-Pacific Partnership">
        Trans-Pacific Partnership
       </a>
       trade agreement, which he called "a continuation of other disastrous
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_agreement" title="Trade agreement">
        trade agreements
       </a>
       , like NAFTA,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic-Central_America_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Dominican Republic-Central America Free Trade Agreement">
        CAFTA
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Permanent_normal_trade_relations" title="Permanent normal trade relations">
        permanent normal trade relations
       </a>
       with China". He believes that free trade agreements have caused a loss of American jobs and depressed American wages. Sanders has said that America needs to rebuild its
       <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">
        manufacturing
       </a>
       base using American factories for well-paying jobs for American labor rather than
       <a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">
        outsourcing
       </a>
       to China and elsewhere.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Policy_of_the_Trump_administration">
        Policy of the Trump administration
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Renegotiation">
        Renegotiation
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Shortly after his
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">
        election
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">
        U.S. President
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">
        Donald Trump
       </a>
       said he would begin renegotiating the terms of NAFTA, to resolve trade issues he had campaigned on. The leaders of
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       have indicated their willingness to work with the Trump administration
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . Although vague on the exact terms he seeks in a renegotiated NAFTA, Trump threatened to withdraw from it if negotiations fail.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 2017, the Trump administration provided a detailed list of changes that it would like to see to NAFTA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:13-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The top priority was a reduction in the United States' trade deficit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_111-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:13-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The administration also called for the elimination of provisions that allowed Canada and Mexico to appeal duties imposed by the United States and limited the ability of the United States to impose import restrictions on Canada and Mexico.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_111-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:13-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The list also alleged subsidized state-owned enterprises and currency manipulation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_111-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-:13-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:14_113-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:14-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to Chad Bown of the Peterson Institute for International Economics, the Trump administration's list "is very consistent with the president's stance on liking trade barriers, liking protectionism. This makes NAFTA in many respects less of a free-trade agreement."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_111-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-:13-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The concerns expressed by the US Trade Representative over subsidized state-owned enterprises and
       <a href="/wiki/Currency_intervention" title="Currency intervention">
        currency manipulation
       </a>
       are not thought to apply to Canada and Mexico, but rather to be designed to send a message to countries beyond North America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_111-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-:13-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Jeffrey Schott of the Peterson Institute for International Economics noted that it would not be possible to conclude renegotiations quickly while also addressing all the concerns on the list.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:14_113-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:14-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He also said that it would be difficult to do anything about trade deficits.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:14_113-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:14-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       An October 2017
       <a href="/wiki/Op-ed" title="Op-ed">
        op-ed
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">
        Toronto
       </a>
       's
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globe_and_Mail" title="Globe and Mail">
         Globe and Mail
        </a>
       </i>
       questioned whether the United States wanted to re-negotiate the agreement or planned to walk away from it no matter what, noting that newly appointed American ambassador
       <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Knight_Craft" title="Kelly Knight Craft">
        Kelly Knight Craft
       </a>
       is married to the owner of
       <a href="/wiki/Joe_Craft" title="Joe Craft">
        Alliance Resource Partners
       </a>
       , a big US coal operation. Canada is implementing a carbon plan, and there is also the matter of a sale of
       <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" title="Bombardier Aerospace">
        Bombardier
       </a>
       jets. "The Americans inserted so many poison pills into last week's talks in Washington that they should have been charged with murder", wrote the columnist,
       <a href="/wiki/John_Ibbitson" title="John Ibbitson">
        John Ibbitson
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       "A number of the proposals that the United States has put on the table have little or no support from the U.S. business and agriculture community. It isn't clear who they're intended to benefit", said John Murphy, vice-president of the U.S. Chamber of Commerce.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CP_115-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CP-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Pat_Roberts" title="Pat Roberts">
        Pat Roberts
       </a>
       , the senior US senator from
       <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">
        Kansas
       </a>
       , called for an outcry against Trump anti-NAFTA moves, saying the "issues affect real jobs, real lives and real people". Kansas is a major agricultural exporter, and farm groups warn that just threatening to leave NAFTA might cause buyers to minimize uncertainty by seeking out non-US sources.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CP_115-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CP-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A fourth round of talks included a U.S. demand for a sunset clause that would end the agreement in five years, unless the three countries agreed to keep it in place, a provision U.S. Commerce Secretary
       <a href="/wiki/Wilbur_Ross" title="Wilbur Ross">
        Wilbur Ross
       </a>
       has said would allow the countries to kill the deal if it was not working. Canadian Prime Minister Justin Trudeau met with the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Committee_on_Ways_and_Means" title="United States House Committee on Ways and Means">
        House Ways and Means Committee
       </a>
       , since Congress would have to pass legislation rolling back the treaty's provisions if Trump tries to withdraw from the pact.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_of_withdrawing_from_NAFTA">
        Impact of withdrawing from NAFTA
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Following Donald Trump's
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">
        election to the presidency
       </a>
       , a range of trade experts have said that pulling out of NAFTA as Trump proposed would have a range of unintended consequences for the U.S., including reduced access to the U.S.'s biggest export markets, a reduction in economic growth, and increased prices for gasoline, cars, fruits, and vegetables.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:10-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The worst affected sectors would be textiles, agriculture and automobiles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:11-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to
       <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">
        Tufts University
       </a>
       political scientist
       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_W._Drezner" title="Daniel W. Drezner">
        Daniel W. Drezner
       </a>
       , the Trump administration's desire to return relations with Mexico to the pre-NAFTA era are misguided. Drezner argues that NAFTA made it easier for Mexico to transform to a real democracy and become a country that views itself as North American. If Trump acts on many of the threats that he has made against Mexico, it is not inconceivable that Mexicans would turn to left-wing populist strongmen, as several South-American countries have. At the very least, US-Mexico relations would worsen, with adverse implications for cooperation on border security, counterterrorism, drug-war cooperation, deportations and managing Central American
       <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">
        migration
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_50-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:7-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to Chad P. Bown (senior fellow at the
       <a href="/wiki/Peterson_Institute_for_International_Economics" title="Peterson Institute for International Economics">
        Peterson Institute for International Economics
       </a>
       ), "a renegotiated NAFTA that would reestablish
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_barrier" title="Trade barrier">
        trade barriers
       </a>
       is unlikely to help workers who lost their jobs—regardless of the cause—take advantage of new employment opportunities".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to Harvard economist
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Melitz" title="Marc Melitz">
        Marc Melitz
       </a>
       , "recent research estimates that the repeal of NAFTA would not increase car production in the United States".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:8-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Melitz notes that this would cost manufacturing jobs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_11-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-:8-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Trans-Pacific_Partnership">
        Trans-Pacific Partnership
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       If the
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership" title="Trans-Pacific Partnership">
        Trans-Pacific Partnership
       </a>
       (TPP) comes into effect, existing agreements such as NAFTA will be reduced to those provisions that do not conflict with the TPP, or that require greater trade liberalization than the TPP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, only
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       will have the prospect of becoming members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership" title="Trans-Pacific Partnership">
        TPP
       </a>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">
        U.S. President
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">
        Donald Trump
       </a>
       withdrew the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       from the agreement in January 2017. In May 2017, the 11 remaining members of the TPP, including Canada and Mexico, agreed to proceed with the trade deal without U.S. participation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">
        See also
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
       <ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
        <li style="display:table-row">
         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emblem-money.svg">
           <img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/28px-Emblem-money.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/42px-Emblem-money.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/56px-Emblem-money.svg.png 2x" width="28"/>
          </a>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Washington+Post&amp;rft.atitle=What+is+NAFTA%2C+and+what+would+happen+to+U.S.+trade+without+it%3F&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.washingtonpost.com%2Fnews%2Fmonkey-cage%2Fwp%2F2017%2F02%2F15%2Fwhat-is-nafta-and-what-would-happen-to-u-s-trade-without-it%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANorth+American+Free+Trade+Agreement">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-119">
